<span id="freeTextContainer8654051967766745325">Another book where the characters dialogue is basically poetry?<br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>You said I was a natural, laughing at all the mortals and their maudlin, trivial lives. . .<br/>This life, my life. . .<br/>It's not trivial.<br/>It's. . . <br/>Mine.<br/>Mine, mine, mine.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>*rolls eyes*</b><br/><br/>I only finished this book because <b>A.)</b> I bought a physical copy and never read it, <b>B.)</b> I liked the cover. <b>Great reasons</b>, <i>I know</i>, but still. And now that I've finished it, it feels like every second spent reading this was a waste. <br/><br/><u>This is me trying to </u></span>
  <span id="freeText8654051967766745325" style="display:none">Another book where the characters dialogue is basically poetry?<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>You said I was a natural, laughing at all the mortals and their maudlin, trivial lives. . .<br />This life, my life. . .<br />It's not trivial.<br />It's. . . <br />Mine.<br />Mine, mine, mine.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>*rolls eyes*</b><br /><br />I only finished this book because <b>A.)</b> I bought a physical copy and never read it, <b>B.)</b> I liked the cover. <b>Great reasons</b>, <i>I know</i>, but still. And now that I've finished it, it feels like every second spent reading this was a waste. <br /><br /><u>This is me trying to explain the plot</u>:<br /><br /><b>Poppy</b> is a cruel, spoiled, and beautiful girl who strings along lots of people, but mainly Midnight. <b>Midnight</b> is her neighbor and totally in love with her, until he moves and decides to break off their messed up friendship (?) He moves in next to <b>Wink</b>, a girl with lots of siblings and who doesn't care for other peoples opinions. <br /><br /><b>Then,</b> Midnight falls for Wink in like .02 seconds.<br /><b>Also,</b> a sort of love triangle happens.<br /><b>And</b> other random confusing stuff happens.<br /><br />The first 10% I didn't like, but then it got a lot better <i>for a little</i> and then took a nosedive. Midnight was always so clueless, Poppy <b>thought</b> she was some sort of mastermind, and Wink had no personality, in my opinion. <br /><br /><b>1 1/2 stars from me.</b> Mainly because <u>the writing really is beautiful</u>, and because I was entertained at certain points where <i>normal conversations</i> were taking place. Somewhere in between the tying a girl to a piano, stories of the unforgivables or something, and Poppy acting like a <b>worse version</b> of Margo from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6442769.Paper_Towns" title="Paper Towns by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Paper Towns</a>, <b>I stopped caring. </b><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1937005472" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1937005472" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1937005472?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-coverporn">z-coverporn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=romance-free">romance-free</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2016">y-out2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=gorgeous-writing">gorgeous-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2017">z-read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=plot-twists">plot-twists</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1937005472" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17102403827306946510">I can't decide how to rate this, so I'm going for a nice, easy three stars. First things first: <b>this is hands down the weirdest book I have ever read.</b> You thought <i>We Were Liars</i> and <i>The Accident Season</i> were weird? <i>Wink Poppy Midnight</i> is far, far weirder, and it's more because of the ending than anything else. <b>Most books at least give you the luxury of a sensical ending. This book does not.</b><br/><br/><i>Wink Poppy Midnight</i> follows two girls, Wink and Poppy, and one boy, Midnight. There's an odd sort of love tri</span>
  <span id="freeText17102403827306946510" style="display:none">I can't decide how to rate this, so I'm going for a nice, easy three stars. First things first: <b>this is hands down the weirdest book I have ever read.</b> You thought <i>We Were Liars</i> and <i>The Accident Season</i> were weird? <i>Wink Poppy Midnight</i> is far, far weirder, and it's more because of the ending than anything else. <b>Most books at least give you the luxury of a sensical ending. This book does not.</b><br /><br /><i>Wink Poppy Midnight</i> follows two girls, Wink and Poppy, and one boy, Midnight. There's an odd sort of love triangle, not like any you're used to. And that's pretty much all I can say about the plot. Yep, this one relies on surprising you. <br /><br />First things first: I loved the <b>subverting of tropes</b> here. Tucholke subverts the typical Betty-and-Veronica dynamic of a love triangle, as well as playing around with the hero-and-villain dynamic. I appreciated that! <br /><br />I liked the <b>writing style</b>, too. At times it began to annoy me slightly, but I can't deny that it made this story incredibly <b>atmospheric.</b><br /><br />Unfortunately, the plot felt a little messy. This happens all the time in magical realism novels; the author is trying to keep things ambiguous, and you end up with a book that's confusing instead. There were moments where I felt like the author succeeded in having something ambiguous yet interesting, and moments where <b>the book wasn't ambiguous, just confusing.</b><br /><br />I've said it before and I'll say it again: it takes a very talented author to keep everything ambiguous but still develop characters well. April Genevieve Tucholke... <i>kind of</i> succeeded. Her characters are as developed as they can be considering the odd style, I guess. <b>Their arcs had wasted potential.</b> The ending underwhelmed me just a bit in terms of character work. <br /><br />I still don't know how I felt about this book, but I recommend giving it a try. It's worth reading if only to have your brain screwed with. <br /><br /><u>Spoiler-Y Notes (skip these!!)</u><br />• I honestly thought at one point the author would have the two girls get together. They literally make out twice in this book. <br />• Everyone says they hated Poppy but I actually kinda liked her in the second half!!<br />• Wink calls herself the hero towards the end, but she's also the liar. So is Midnight the villain?</span>
  <a data-text-id="17102403827306946510" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2299500157" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2299500157" />
    <a title="Micah Francis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33809095-micah-francis"><img alt="Micah Francis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421623478p2/33809095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2299500157?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Micah Francis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Micah Francis" href="/user/show/33809095-micah-francis">Micah Francis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33809095-micah-francis?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33809095-micah-francis?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2299500157&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2299500157" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17084276142262361532">I give this book 3.5 stars. It had me hooked from the beginning and I could not put it down. In part this was due to the way it was written. No chapters. Sections narrated by each character and they would give me just enough information to make me want more and keep reading. Then THE THING happens. There was so much build up until this and afterwards it just felt anticlimactic. I was surprised to find out what happened but not in a good way. It was more of a I feel let down, and that’s it? kind </span>
  <span id="freeText17084276142262361532" style="display:none">I give this book 3.5 stars. It had me hooked from the beginning and I could not put it down. In part this was due to the way it was written. No chapters. Sections narrated by each character and they would give me just enough information to make me want more and keep reading. Then THE THING happens. There was so much build up until this and afterwards it just felt anticlimactic. I was surprised to find out what happened but not in a good way. It was more of a I feel let down, and that’s it? kind of feeling. I did enjoy the writing style and the magical realism feel to the book. I wish the magical realism would have been explored more. It served no purpose in this book except for the seance scene. Wink’s narratives hinted toward magical realism that was never explored. Such as the fairies and the unforgivables. Again, the ending felt anticlimactic and made the entire experience in the Luck house feel as if it were all for nothing. I felt that issues were left unaddressed and unanswered. I was left with questions and feeling slightly confused. That being said, I did mostly enjoy this book and I may try to read it again later. I would like to give this author another try. Hopefully, other people will enjoy this book more than I did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17084276142262361532" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="A.G. Howard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5920436-a-g-howard"><img alt="A.G. Howard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566101899p2/5920436.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1364625538?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="A.G. Howard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="A.G. Howard" href="/user/show/5920436-a-g-howard">A.G. Howard</a>
      </span>

          marked it as to-read




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1364625538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11422688280078783590">That cover is gorgeous and chaotic and luscious. Also, anything April writes is beautiful and eerie. CANNOT wait for this one! <3 </span>
  <span id="freeText11422688280078783590" style="display:none">That cover is gorgeous and chaotic and luscious. Also, anything April writes is beautiful and eerie. CANNOT wait for this one! &lt;3 </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer988159318066256965"><i>Wink kissed deep. Deep as a dark, misty, forest path. One that lead to blood and love and death and monsters</i><br/><br/>Disclaimer: **I may have been harsh here but I didn’t give up on April Genevieve Tucholke with this being my first of hers and I am SOOO GLAD because <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2144379319' rel='nofollow noopener'>BETWEEN THE DEVIL AND THE DEEP BLUE SEA</a> is everything to me!!!   <span id="freeText988159318066256965" style="display:none"><i>Wink kissed deep. Deep as a dark, misty, forest path. One that lead to blood and love and death and monsters</i><br /><br />Disclaimer: **I may have been harsh here but I didn’t give up on April Genevieve Tucholke with this being my first of hers and I am SOOO GLAD because <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2144379319" rel="nofollow noopener">BETWEEN THE DEVIL AND THE DEEP BLUE SEA</a> is everything to me!!! Read it now!!!!! <br /><br /><br />This book.....I don’t even know what the heck I just read......<br /><br />I even *almost* read it all in one go, I stayed up real, real late into the night with it. But then I realised that it wasn’t that I was enthralled but that I was like angry-reading wanting something to actually freaking happen. <br /><br />Have you ever angry-read before? <br /><br />It’s not a great feeling. <br /><br />It’s like you’re mad because you know you’re wasting your time and you know you should give up but for some reason you can’t stop reading, because you’re harbouring a spark of hope for redemption. <br /><br />But then redemption never comes. And you wake up the next morning looking like death because you traded precious beauty sleep all for nothing. <br /><br />That’s what this book is. What it was for me. <br /><br />I wish it was exactly like the quote up there. I wish I would’ve known this was such a contemporary and not anything else (how did I miss that??). <br />But for some reason I thought it was something else. <br /><br />And as I was reading I hated it. And I kept thinking ugh this is like those pointless books my mum used to pass off on me when I was in my teen years. But I couldn’t place what it was. <br /><br />It’s contemporary. That’s what. <br /><br />Ugh. <br /><br />I wanted to like this. Even with the smidge of ghost stories and tarot reading and stormy summer nights with stolen kisses. <br /><br />But I was so damn pissed off at the characters. And then the twist was like, oh come on really? <br /><br />Toss the book at the wall. <br /><br />At least it’s pretty. <br /><br />I’m out.</span>

<div id="review_1834725443" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1834725443" />
    <a title="Annamaria " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24195966-annamaria"><img alt="Annamaria " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487070187p2/24195966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1834725443?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annamaria " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annamaria " href="/user/show/24195966-annamaria">Annamaria </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24195966-annamaria?shelf=read-in-english">read-in-english</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1834725443" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4366545820859132016">"<b>She was bad.<br/>And she was good.<br/>She was real.</b>"<br/><br/>This was... underwhelming. I don't even know why I decided to pick this one up, maybe because I read <i>magical realism</i> and thought I haven't had any of that this year and needed a fix as soon as I could or maybe because I wanted a nice cover to end my Goodreads challenge with. I don't know, I just know this book was not what I had been looking for.<br/><br/><b>Every story needs a hero.<br/>Every story needs a villain.<br/>Every story needs a secret.</b><br/><br/>I dare each one of you to te</span>
  <span id="freeText4366545820859132016" style="display:none">"<b>She was bad.<br>And she was good.<br>She was real.</b>"<br><br>This was... underwhelming. I don't even know why I decided to pick this one up, maybe because I read <i>magical realism</i> and thought I haven't had any of that this year and needed a fix as soon as I could or maybe because I wanted a nice cover to end my Goodreads challenge with. I don't know, I just know this book was not what I had been looking for.<br><br><b>Every story needs a hero.<br>Every story needs a villain.<br>Every story needs a secret.</b><br><br>I dare each one of you to tell me that you wouldn't be intrigued by those lines. What do they mean? What's the <i>secret</i>?? The problem though is that this book is not intriguing at all, the plot is so very thin that I kept asking myself why the author thought it was an acceptable one for a whole new book. Why not a short story? A novella maybe? But a book? The story was so watered-down that I was going claustrophobic, <i>when was it going to end</i>??? <br><br>Here we have <u>Wink</u>, the quirky girl next door, <u>Poppy</u>, the bully, the mean girl, and <u>Midnight</u>, who's hopelessly in love with Poppy, but who settles for the friend(ish) with benefits. Wink is obsessed with a fantasy book series and convinces Midnight of being the hero of his own story. He needs to step up to Poppy, the beast to be tamed and slayed. How do they manage that? When Poppy tries to convince Midnight to play a cruel prank on Wink, our <s>spineless</s> Hero, instead of just refusing her, proceedes to join forces with Wink and prank Poppy instead. The prank being tying the girl to a chair in a haunted house and leaving her there all night long. Because what says Hero more than psychologically torture a teenage girl albeit cruel and willing to play that very prank on another person?<br><br><blockquote>"<i>I'd never get the sound of her screams out of my head, or my heart.<br>Is this what it meant to be the hero?</i>"</blockquote><br><br>No idiot, what kind of definition of "hero" does you dictionary have? Aren't you educated at all?? What kind of idiot is so blinded by his sense of entitlement, of hatred and the <i>oh, friendzoned again!</i> feelings that he needs to do something so mean and then even justify himself?? Poppy was mean, intolerable, pretentious, borderline narcisistic and a sociopath but you, my dear Midnight, you had to simply reject her, to simply will yourself to shut her out of your life, not leaving the windows of your bedroom wide open to then say "Oh well, she's in my bedroom now, I might as well sleep with her while plotting her demise!". I'm disgusted.<br><br>And, you might say, ok then you didn't like the plot but the <i>secret</i>? What about it? Oh, my friend, if only I even knew. Sure, I understand it, I understand that the underlying meaning of this story is to tell me that people are not just a façade, they are not just what they decide to show to the world. Mainly they're what they don't tell, what they keep inside. But after all that turmoil, after having supposedly caused a mental breakdown in a girl to then lack the emotional depth to understand that something went wrong in this Wink/Midnight partnership I couldn't care less.<br><br>The writing was poetic at times, but I couldn't take it very seriously.<br><br>"<b>Wink kissed deep. Deep as a dark, misty, forest path. One that lead to blood and love and death and monsters.</b>"<br>^ How do you <i>kiss deep as a forest path</i>? Do I need an upgrade? <br><br>In conclusion, I really didn't get the hype around this book but I've also seen that it has been enjoyed by several other readers so it might make a different impression in you than it did in me. <br><br><u>Summarizing the book in one tweet though:</u><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481455982i/21423204._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="4366545820859132016" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1547708858" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16091321830804435197">This was definitely one of the weirdest books I've read in a while. When I first started, it was very clear who the "hero" was and who the "villain" was. As I learned more about the characters and got completely involved with this story, my opinions changed and I couldn't pin point ANY of these characters. I trusted NONE of them and the story constantly kept me thinking and on my toes. The villain slowly started becoming innocent, the innocent one started becoming the villain but also the hero..</span>
  <span id="freeText16091321830804435197" style="display:none">This was definitely one of the weirdest books I've read in a while. When I first started, it was very clear who the "hero" was and who the "villain" was. As I learned more about the characters and got completely involved with this story, my opinions changed and I couldn't pin point ANY of these characters. I trusted NONE of them and the story constantly kept me thinking and on my toes. The villain slowly started becoming innocent, the innocent one started becoming the villain but also the hero...this was definitely a thought provoking read. Five stars all the way! </span>
  <a data-text-id="16091321830804435197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1650633760" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1650633760" />
    <a title="Michelle (Pink Polka Dot Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6159720-michelle-pink-polka-dot-books"><img alt="Michelle (Pink Polka Dot Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529478068p2/6159720.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1650633760?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle (Pink Polka Dot Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle (Pink Polka Dot Books)" href="/user/show/6159720-michelle-pink-polka-dot-books">Michelle (Pink Polka Dot Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1650633760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13378275264910078638"><b>3.5 or 4 stars??? Hard decision. I'm not sure I "get" books like these. This was an odd fairy tale of a book w/ a cool atmosphere, but with characters that feel fictional.</b><br/><br/><i>This is the story of 3 teens-- Wink, Poppy, and Midnight. Midnight has been in love with Poppy for years, but Poppy is all about Poppy. Now he's moved in next door to Wink and her large, wild family. Wink is child-like and tells fairy tales, and something about her interests Midnight. He's also desperate to get over Poppy, and </i></span>
  <span id="freeText13378275264910078638" style="display:none"><b>3.5 or 4 stars??? Hard decision. I'm not sure I "get" books like these. This was an odd fairy tale of a book w/ a cool atmosphere, but with characters that feel fictional.</b><br><br><i>This is the story of 3 teens-- Wink, Poppy, and Midnight. Midnight has been in love with Poppy for years, but Poppy is all about Poppy. Now he's moved in next door to Wink and her large, wild family. Wink is child-like and tells fairy tales, and something about her interests Midnight. He's also desperate to get over Poppy, and she's all too happy to help him get revenge on "the Wolf" (Poppy).<br><br>In this story nothing is as it seems. Events unfold, but it's unclear what intentions each of the character's have. It'll keep you guessing-- Who exactly is the hero of this book?</i><br><br><b>My Thoughts:</b><br>First of all this book was giving me MAJOR Cover Lust. It's pretty much the whole reason I wanted to read the book. I actually just want them to print this design on a dress or a pair of shoes so I can wear it. While this is the perfect cover for the story, the cover was definitely the best part of this book for me.<br><br>I'm not sure I actually "get" books like this. It's kind of just about 3 teens who run around in the woods/courtryside and in 2016, I find it a little hard to relate to. Don't get me wrong, I know there are all different kinds of people out there, but I kind of want/expect YA's to act like YA's a little bit. When I was in my prime teen years cell phones were just coming in, the internet was dial-up, and there was no social media-- but we did NOT run around in the woods. We begged our parents for their cars and drove around. We went to underage dance clubs, tried to find someone who would buy us beer, and tried to figure out where all the boys were hanging out. We sat in our bedrooms and watched MTV and called each other to talk about the newest music videos. Obviously times have changed a little bit from that, but still....<br><br>The thing about this book is it's all about atmosphere, not about plot. And it's a pretty cool atmosphere to immerse yourself in if you can let yourself go in it. I don't think I'm one of those people though. I need order and sense and explanations in my stories. I don't think I'm SUPER rigid, but I'm not as go-with-the-flow as this book needed me to be. The writing was great-- it gave the book just the right feel that it needed, but I need more than cool writing and beautiful prose to get involved in a story.<br><br>It's hard to talk about anything that happens in the book because you kind of need to NOT know in order to fully enjoy it. Because the people start out one way and by the end they supposedly change into something else?? At least that's what I got out of it. It's basically a "modern day" fairy tale where you can't trust who the good guys and bad guys are. But in the end I just ended up kind of confused, so if someone who read this wants to explain it to me, I'd be down to talk.<br><br>One thing for sure is-- I HATED Poppy. Not matter what happened and where she ended up, I still hate her and I really don't think there is anything the author could do to make me feel otherwise. Everything Leif says about her, I was nodding my head like crazy.<br><br><b>OVERALL: I liked reading something different, but I just don't "get" books like this. It's fairy tale-like and full of atmosphere, but I wanted more. I think a lot of people would be into this type of book because it's so different, but I need more order and sense in my books. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17675462.The_Raven_Boys__The_Raven_Cycle___1_" title="The Raven Boys (The Raven Cycle, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven Boys</a> is a series that has these elements, but has a lot more story. I would more recommend that if you are looking for this type of book.<br><br>My Blog:</b><br><a href="http://www.pinkpolkadotbooks.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453193263i/17792886.png" alt="Pink Polka Dot Books" width="225" height="141" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="13378275264910078638" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6113135746077726108">This review can also be found at <a href='http://carolesrandomlife.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Carole's Random Life</a>.<br/><br/>I hate to say that I am a little bit disappointed with this book. That doesn't mean that this was a bad book. Not at all. It just wasn't what I had hoped it would be. I had really high hopes for this book and bumped it to the front of my TBR pile so it is really quite possible that some of my disappointment is simply a result of unrealistic expectations. <br/><br/>This story is told from three point of views. Wink is one of the Bell children. She is a </span>
  <span id="freeText6113135746077726108" style="display:none">This review can also be found at <a href="http://carolesrandomlife.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Carole's Random Life</a>.<br /><br />I hate to say that I am a little bit disappointed with this book. That doesn't mean that this was a bad book. Not at all. It just wasn't what I had hoped it would be. I had really high hopes for this book and bumped it to the front of my TBR pile so it is really quite possible that some of my disappointment is simply a result of unrealistic expectations. <br /><br />This story is told from three point of views. Wink is one of the Bell children. She is a sweet girl with curly red hair who lives across the street from Midnight. Midnight is a genuinely nice boy who has just moved into a crooked little house across the street from Wink with his father. Poppy is a bully who likes to push people around and manipulate Midnight every chance she gets.<br /><br />I did like the way the story was laid with with quick chapters told from the perspectives of the three main characters. The story really felt like a fairy tale in a lot of ways. The voices of the characters were very distinctive as well as interesting. I wouldn't really say that I grew to like any of them though. There was just no connection for me. Of course, I am an old lady that barely remembers what it was like to be a teenager anymore.<br /><br />I knew going into the book that there would be a secret and someone in the story might be lying from reading the description. It is even on the cover of the book. I guess I was hoping for some kind of epic event to happen but in the end I was never very excited about anything that actually happened in the book. I would even say that I was a bit bored at times. <br /><br />I do think that a lot of people will probably enjoy this book. It just didn't work for me. This is the first book by April Genevieve Tucholke and I would be very interested in trying one of her other novels since there were aspects of her writing style that I did enjoy. <br /><br /><i>I received an advance reader edition of this book from Penguin Publishing Group - Dial Books via First to Read for the purpose of providing an honest review.</i><br /><br /><b>Initial Thoughts</b><br />I have to say that I am a little let down by this book. It wasn't bad but it wasn't what I thought it would be at all. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17613027898118152832">I loved April's other books, so it goes without saying that I was beyond eager to get my greedy hands on her new words.<br/><br/>Wink, Poppy, and Midnight are all such different characters. I loved the sharp, staccato chapters. Not to mention her gorgeous and atmospheric prose. I want to </span>
  <span id="freeText17613027898118152832" style="display:none">I loved April's other books, so it goes without saying that I was beyond eager to get my greedy hands on her new words.<br /><br />Wink, Poppy, and Midnight are all such different characters. I loved the sharp, staccato chapters. Normally, I can't stand more than 2 POVs, but I was craving each character to tell me what was going on from their side.<br /><br />The plot was twisty and intriguing and filled with mindfuckery in a way that only April can give us. Not to mention her gorgeous and atmospheric prose. I want to live in her words and never come out.<br /><br />With this story, she has officially become an author whose grocery list I will read. </span>

<div id="review_1529797171" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1529797171" />
    <a title="Kels" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28386116-kels"><img alt="Kels" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466351542p2/28386116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1529797171?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kels" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kels" href="/user/show/28386116-kels">Kels</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28386116-kels?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28386116-kels?shelf=mixed-feelings">mixed-feelings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28386116-kels?shelf=alternating-povs">alternating-povs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28386116-kels?shelf=gritty">gritty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28386116-kels?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28386116-kels?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28386116-kels?shelf=face-stuck-in-book">face-stuck-in-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28386116-kels?shelf=lazy-day-reads">lazy-day-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28386116-kels?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28386116-kels?shelf=easy-read">easy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1529797171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17144634957460389197">WHAAATTT did I just read?! Because I'm still not sure.... and oddly enough, I'm okay with that. Kind of.<br/><br/>Warning: this review is deliberately ambiguous, and I'm not even sorry. <br/><br/>In truth, I picked up this novel simply because of the gorgeous cover. Yep. I'm a sucker like that <s>sometimes</s> always. But come on. Just look at that cover!! Now picture it on a book shelf. Now picture it on YOUR book shelf.... am I right, or <i>amIright</i>? <br/><br/>When I first started this book, a few pages in and I didn't think it was </span>
  <span id="freeText17144634957460389197" style="display:none">WHAAATTT did I just read?! Because I'm still not sure.... and oddly enough, I'm okay with that. Kind of.<br /><br />Warning: this review is deliberately ambiguous, and I'm not even sorry. <br /><br />In truth, I picked up this novel simply because of the gorgeous cover. Yep. I'm a sucker like that <s>sometimes</s> always. But come on. Just look at that cover!! Now picture it on a book shelf. Now picture it on YOUR book shelf.... am I right, or <i>amIright</i>? <br /><br />When I first started this book, a few pages in and I didn't think it was a book meant for me to read. Just check my status updates. I simply wasn't sold on the characters. My initial reactions to meeting them were to roll my eyes, because what kids talk like Poppy? Or act like Midnight? Or think like Wink? (haha, didn't mean for that last one to rhyme. Bear with me folks. It's been a long night.) And what's up with their names? So yeah, I had my concerns. On top of that, I wasn't sure where the plot was going, if there even was one. BUT I persisted!<br /><br />The writing, simply put, deserves applause. It's beautiful, quirky, atmospheric, and filled with the personality of the three main characters. It has that magical realism vibe to it, but there's something more to Tucholke's writing that I find hard to put into words. As I mentioned above, I almost put this book down, but slowly and then suddenly my face was buried in the text. I found it extremely hard to pry myself away from this story because I had become so captivated by it and so enraptured by the characters. I MISSED LUNCH, because I forgot that I'm human and I need to eat and I LOVE FOOD so this doesn't happen often for me, is what I'm saying. <br /><br />While I did end up warming up to all of the characters and their eccentric quirks, the plot steadily confused me from start to finish. It's not that it was hard to follow, I just didn't see the point in the trail. There's a lot of events that don't seem to lead up to anything. But just wait for it: cause holy cow, THAT PLOT TWIST, was so freaking unexpected. I mean, what even? It had me scratching my head in contemplation, because I thought I got it, but then was I wrong, and my brain felt overworked in the process, and this is one very long run-on sentence. Okay. Moving on to the ending... it wasn't my favorite. Quite honestly, the second half ruined a lot of my enjoyment. I just don't think it all added up in the ending.<br /><br />Okay, okay, I know this was such a rambling excuse of a review (can't say I didn't warn you) but walking into this story was an experience, and I don't want to deprive anyone who might decide to pick up this book in the future of sharing in that mysterious allure. This was a very quick, deliciously peculiar novel. I would definitely suggest that you be in the mood for a strange read before picking this one up. Overall, I'm quite happy that I gave this novel a shot. It certainly did impress me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17144634957460389197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8950014623021278218" style="display:none">First of all: I want to thank Fransinda for doing this buddyread with me. I love doing buddyreads, where you can share your thoughts with another booklover while reading. Second of all.. WHAT is this low Goodreads score?! I can't believe it. Sadly I also have a life and I had to work and stuff *grumble*. The book was a favorite for the both of us. The poetic way it's written, the way it's small and big at the same time together with the mystery is a treat to read!</span>

<div id="review_1284781752" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1284781752" />
    <a title="Rashika (is tired)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8492956-rashika-is-tired"><img alt="Rashika (is tired)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476647072p2/8492956.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1284781752?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rashika (is tired)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rashika (is tired)" href="/user/show/8492956-rashika-is-tired">Rashika (is tired)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=realistic-contemporary">realistic-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=mind-blown">mind-blown</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=good-characters">good-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=pub-penguin">pub-penguin</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1284781752" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15085509046514744800"><b>
  <i>***This review has also been posted on <a href='http://wp.me/p3p0qg-1MV' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Social Potato</a></i>
</b><br/><br/>I don’t even know how to react to this book. It takes you on a twisty, surreal journey and leaves your brain scrambled. So what actually happened? That is a good question. DON’T ASK ME. I might be lying and you would never know. Oops.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Likes</u>
</b><br/><br/><b>Creepiness:</b> While this book may sound like a mystery/contemporary, it is also deliciously creepy. There is so much that readers are in the dark about but it’s done in a way that isn’t frustrating. </span>
  <span id="freeText15085509046514744800" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>***This review has also been posted on <a href="http://wp.me/p3p0qg-1MV" rel="nofollow noopener">The Social Potato</a></i>
</b><br /><br />I don’t even know how to react to this book. It takes you on a twisty, surreal journey and leaves your brain scrambled. So what actually happened? That is a good question. DON’T ASK ME. I might be lying and you would never know. Oops.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Likes</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Creepiness:</b> While this book may sound like a mystery/contemporary, it is also deliciously creepy. There is so much that readers are in the dark about but it’s done in a way that isn’t frustrating. It’s exciting, engaging and FITTING with the characters and the vibe the book has going.<br /><br /><b>Unreliable narrators:</b> I love me some unreliable narrators and this book definitely delivered on that end. I had a hard time deciding who I wanted to trust because even though there was one character that was horrible, the other two had hidden depths to them that made me wary of them. Basically, don’t trust anybody when reading this book. ALL THE CHARACTERS ARE GOING TO FUCK WITH YOUR MIND.<br /><br /><b>MIND FUCKERY:</b> The caps lock is necessary when talking about the mind fuckery in the book. This ties back into my previous point about unreliable narrators. It’s hard to keep up with all the twists happening in the book because it get’s so twisty. My brain felt like a pretzel after I had finished the book.<br /><br /><b>Writing Style:</b> I thought the division of the different point of views in this book worked very well. The characters did sound similar sometimes but I thought it was intentional because it helped confuse me even more about what the characters were doing/thinking/plotting.<br /><br /><b>My shippy feels:</b> Of course I had shippy feels. I AM TRASH (this does not mean you are trash if you have shippy feels. I’ve just taken to referring myself as trash because I think the word trash describes me perfectly). Mind you, not all the relationships in this book were healthy and weren't meant to be. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Dislikes</u>
</b><br /><br />My only dislike is that I wasn’t satisfied with the big revelation. I felt like there were things that didn’t add up. I love my twists but if I cannot trace back to places where I should have seen it coming or trace the story-line, the reveal won't work for me. And this reveal unfortunately didn't. The reveal also somewhat spoiled my reading experience because I went from being on a 'book high' to being annoyed. <br /><br />But if you like psychological thrillers, or books that turn your mind into a pretzel, Wink Poppy Midnight is for you.<br /><br /><i>Note that I received an advanced copy of this book in exchange for an honest review</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15085509046514744800" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1739062963" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1739062963" />
    <a title="Roshani Chokshi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26262898-roshani-chokshi"><img alt="Roshani Chokshi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544538349p2/26262898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1739062963?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roshani Chokshi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roshani Chokshi" href="/user/show/26262898-roshani-chokshi">Roshani Chokshi</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1739062963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9112725447450471168">Oh...my...<br/><br/>This book. This clever, clever book. Tucholke's language is dreamy and creepy, and even though this feels like a ghost story it's a brilliant contemporary. This is a story about people that have to try on different identities before they finally fit inside themselves. <br/><br/>Highly recommend. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dAJZxCmoee+hzfNzanTj9Vqlx9PNuBTvx+g6HzURGtbLBsUEaaFXIMWnKcxHGsYxaCew2t+txGo9gkE3XJCweg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fgO+hQk0Av/GrvG9ltsFUNtXcZS5tO3wu/BRdrJ2YfDBByJFST0sMKLEKwK7tSCU6dUGnauhPXVBmipe2/fLXA==')})
  }

        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_50358142').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_50358142').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3176551183898087577">April Genevieve Tucholke is the author of <i>Between the Devil and the Deep Blue Sea,</i> <i>Between the Spark and the Burn,</i> <i>Wink Poppy Midnight</i>, <i>The Boneless Mercies,</i> and <i>Seven Endless Forests.</i> She also curated the horror anthology <i>Slasher Girls & Monster Boys</i>. Her books have been published in sixteen countries, and have received ten starred reviews. They have been selected for the Junior Library Guild, Ki</span>
  <span id="freeText3176551183898087577" style="display:none">April Genevieve Tucholke is the author of <i>Between the Devil and the Deep Blue Sea,</i> <i>Between the Spark and the Burn,</i> <i>Wink Poppy Midnight</i>, <i>The Boneless Mercies,</i> and <i>Seven Endless Forests.</i> She also curated the horror anthology <i>Slasher Girls &amp; Monster Boys</i>. Her books have been published in sixteen countries, and have received ten starred reviews. They have been selected for the Junior Library Guild, Kids' Indie Next picks, and YALSA Teens Top Ten. When she's not writing, April likes walking in the woods, exploring abandoned houses, and drinking expensive coffee. She currently resides in the Pacific Northwest with her husband.</span>
